  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8b1fbb6e-b894-4106-976d-a57148ad659e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer16428735722549613629">In her second year of mourning, lovely, young widow Passion Elizabeth Dare never dreamed she would be with a man again—and certainly not a complete stranger.   <span id="freeText16428735722549613629" style="display:none">In her second year of mourning, lovely, young widow Passion Elizabeth Dare never dreamed she would be with a man again—and certainly not a complete stranger. But amidst the crowds of London's Crystal Palace, Passion finds herself discreetly, yet insistently, pursued by a sensual gentleman who awakens her long-supressed desires. After a loveless marriage of restrained propriety, Passion abandons herself to true bliss for the first time.<br /><br />Intoxicated by his encounter with the beautiful stranger, Mark Randolph Hawkmore, Earl of Langley, cannot wait to see her again. As a series of rapturous rendezvous follows, he and his mystery lover find something rare and wonderful blossoming between them. But a blackmail scheme against the Earl threatens to destroy everything. As a scandal brews, each will have to choose between duty and desire...their love for their families—and their love for each other.</span>

<div id="review_69475779" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69475779" />
    <a title="Ridley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2543252-ridley"><img alt="Ridley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251681007p2/2543252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69475779?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ridley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ridley" href="/user/show/2543252-ridley">Ridley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=read-2009">read-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=paper">paper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=debut">debut</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69475779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15773710463851703344">This book made me wonder if I read the same book that the 5-star reviewers did.<br/><br/>What dreck!<br/><br/>I am by no means squeamish. I lurve the trashy erotic romance, I do, and the hotter the better. Unfortunately, Passion wasn't hot, it was merely profane. I have never read sex scenes that have left me quite so cold.<br/><br/>The plot, when we're treated to it, is fairly tight and satisfying. Valdez does create a sticky situation for the hero, forcing him to choose between his beloved brother and the woman he's grown </span>
  <span id="freeText15773710463851703344" style="display:none">This book made me wonder if I read the same book that the 5-star reviewers did.<br /><br />What dreck!<br /><br />I am by no means squeamish. I lurve the trashy erotic romance, I do, and the hotter the better. Unfortunately, Passion wasn't hot, it was merely profane. I have never read sex scenes that have left me quite so cold.<br /><br />The plot, when we're treated to it, is fairly tight and satisfying. Valdez does create a sticky situation for the hero, forcing him to choose between his beloved brother and the woman he's grown to love. Passion - and I'm sorry, but that name is just straight-up <s>retarded</s> ridiculous - is also in a bind, as Mark is engaged to her cousin, who she's quite fond of. Valdez certainly did put both her and heroine in a tough spot, pitting them against family they loved.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the sexxoring takes up 50-60%+ of the novel, and it is DREADFUL. It's laugh-out-loud ridiculous at times with gems like, "I think my cock is in love with you." I'm sorry, if a man said that to me, I'd laugh in his face and tell him to put his pants back on. The dialog was heavily anachronistic and profane to the point of absurdity. I'm a friggin' working-class hockey fan and I don't drop the F-bomb half as much as these two do, yet I'm supposed to believe this is how an earl and a gentlewoman spoke 150+ years ago?<br /><br />Laughable dialog aside, there was the overly clinical sex. Valdez got her money's worth out of the word cervix, seeing as how it appeared multiple times in every sex scene. Sorry honey, cervix is not a sexy word, especially so when you're making a big deal about this guy's giant schlong banging against it. That sounds painful. I've never winced so much at sex; I was holding a bag of frozen peas to my cooter in sympathy pains.<br /><br />There was a total lack of sexual tension, since they were banging non-stop, and the romance plot was so relegated to the background that the scant emotional conflict simply could not save this train-wreck. <br /><br />Really, if you're going to write an erotic romance, shouldn't the sex be erotic?</span>
  <a data-text-id="15773710463851703344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81649521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81649521" />
    <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish"><img alt="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398981306p2/1113032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81649521?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer81649521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15287831239272985695"><br/><i>
  <b>5 passionate, scintillating, erotic stars!</b>
</i><br/><br/>I absolutely loved this book, though I don’t know if I can put into words all the reasons why and do this story justice because it’s more than just a book...It’s an exciting escape into sexual fantasy, a touching love story, and a <i>happily ever after</i> to rival the best of them.<br/><br/><b>Description…</b><blockquote> In her second year of mourning, lovely, young widow Passion Elizabeth Dare never dreamed she would be with a man again—and certainly not a complete stranger. But ami</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15287831239272985695" style="display:none"><br /><i>
  <b>5 passionate, scintillating, erotic stars!</b>
</i><br /><br />I absolutely loved this book, though I don’t know if I can put into words all the reasons why and do this story justice because it’s more than just a book...It’s an exciting escape into sexual fantasy, a touching love story, and a <i>happily ever after</i> to rival the best of them.<br /><br /><b>Description…</b><blockquote> In her second year of mourning, lovely, young widow Passion Elizabeth Dare never dreamed she would be with a man again—and certainly not a complete stranger. But amidst the crowds of London's Crystal Palace, Passion finds herself discreetly, yet insistently, pursued by a sensual gentleman who awakens her long-supressed desires. After a loveless marriage of restrained propriety, Passion abandons herself to true bliss for the first time.<br /><br />Intoxicated by his encounter with the beautiful stranger, Mark Randolph Hawkmore, Earl of Langley, cannot wait to see her again. As a series of rapturous rendezvous follows, he and his mystery lover find something rare and wonderful blossoming between them. But a blackmail scheme against the Earl threatens to destroy everything. As a scandal brews, each will have to choose between duty and desire...their love for their families—and their love for each other.</blockquote><b>My review contains minor spoilers…</b><br /><br />From the beginning, I was hooked! The prologue alone grabbed my attention and had me thinking <i>Hmmm… there’s going to be trouble in paradise…</i> Then chapter one starts off with one of the most passionate sexual encounters I’ve ever read, between two people who had never before met, in a place where the odds are very good that they’ll get caught. Talk about hot! These few pages alone made this book worth buying. <br /><br />Now let’s talk about the main characters themselves, whom I adore. Mark and Passion are total opposites, but we know what they say about opposites attracting, right? Mark is one of those heroes that I am instantly drawn to; the kind who has built a fortress around his heart, not believing that true love can exist between a man and a woman, and especially not for him. Other than his father and his brother Matt, Mark has never cared for anyone and doesn’t believe that anyone, except for them, has ever cared about him. He is bored with society and cynical – trusting very few people. It’s as if he is <i>in</i> the world, but not truly part of it. He functions, going about his daily life and enjoying his work as a respected architect, but the feeling I get is that he’s a man who stands back and watches while everyone else lives and he merely exists. <br /><br />Passion is the eldest daughter of a “man of the cloth” and was named for Passion Sunday, the day on which she was born. She is a widow who is just about to come out of a long, 2 year mourning. Her marriage was not a good one, and their sex life was dismal – well, hers was. Her husband seemed to enjoy himself rather frequently, and with everyone but Passion. She’s in no hurry to remarry which is part of the reason she stayed in mourning so much longer – according to her aunt – than was <i>necessary</i>. <br /><br />Fortunately for them, <i>and us</i>, a most <u>un</u>fortunate turn of events bring Mark and Passion together in an exhibit hall at the Crystal Palace where they find themselves inexplicably drawn to one another. Their curiosity, desire and longing for something…<i>different</i>… sweeps them up in a torrent of passion where they share their bodies in an uninhibited, almost primitive, need for sexual fulfillment. Their encounter leaves them both sated and yet hungry for more, but having parted without even exchanging names, they may never again see one another. After returning to their homes that day, they are unable to forget their encounter and are left wondering what might happen next – if that passion could possibly be recaptured. They both, each on their own, decide to return to the Crystal Palace the next day in hopes of meeting again and finding out if they can repeat what they had shared, or if it was just a onetime marvel. They were not disappointed at this second meeting – or at the many that followed. The storyline itself is excellent! I love the suspense, the betrayals, the grief, the scheming and most importantly, the deep family ties that see these amazing people through all the heartache they must go through. And when all is said and done, they are so much stronger for having endured it.<br /><br />In addition to Mark and Passion, we have Matthew, Mark’s brother as well as Patience and Primrose who are Passion’s sisters and will be featured in their own books. And we can’t forget poor cousin Charlotte who is her mother’s pawn through all this and well deserving of her own story. All of these characters are warm, loving people who I adore. Another person I came to care about is John Crossman, a young man who had begun to have feelings for Passion, but quickly realized, even before she did, that her heart was bound elsewhere. I hope to see him play a prominent role in future books and would be thrilled if he found his own <i>happily ever after</i> in one of them.<br /><br />I really can’t stress enough that this book should not be looked at as just another erotic novel where page after page is devoted to words describing sexual acts. Though the sexual tension in this book is through the roof amazing and the writing of those scenes is breathtakingly erotic and primitive – it’s so much more than that. This is a heartwarming story about 2 lonely people who, as the walls they have built around their hearts finally begin to crumble, find in one another that one other person in the world who can fill their soul’s emptiness and make them whole again. <br /><br /><b>The bottom line…</b><br /><br />It’s not often that I find a book where I adore both the hero and heroine equally, but <i>Passion</i> is one of those rare instances where it all comes together perfectly for me. And while, as I've said, the sensuality of this book is amazing, it's Mark and Passion's relationship that has given them a place on my list of all time favorite couples and made this a 5 star read. I will come back to this book again and again just to have the chance to spend time with them.<br /><br />One last thing - I just read the excerpt for <i>Patience</i> at the end of the book and let me just say... you don't want to miss that. So when you finish reading <i>Passion</i>, keep turning the pages for the excerpt of <i>Patience.</i> ***fanning myself***<br /><br /><b>Sexual Content:</b> While this book is loaded with sexual situations and very erotic, there is no ménage, anal sex or BDSM.<br /><br /><b>Note:</b> Lisa Valdez answered some questions about why there was such a long time span between <i>Passion</i> and <i>Patience</i> and gave us some information about her 3rd novel in the quartet, <i>Primrose</i>. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://kbgbabbles.blogspot.com/2010/04/lisa-valdez-interview-and-patience-book.html">http://kbgbabbles.blogspot.com/2010/0...</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5429533724831641046">5+ Stars<br/><br/>To me, Passion felt like two completely different books.<br/><br/>For the first 10o pages or so, I found myself caught up in the incredibly vivid and passionate secret love affair between Passion Dare (the heroine's name is beyond silly, but I got used to it) and the intense Mark Randolph Hawkmore. <br/><br/>Literally from the first sentence of this novel, the sexual chemistry and heat generated by these two characters is enough to render a person speechless.   <span id="freeText5429533724831641046" style="display:none">5+ Stars<br /><br />To me, Passion felt like two completely different books.<br /><br />For the first 10o pages or so, I found myself caught up in the incredibly vivid and passionate secret love affair between Passion Dare (the heroine's name is beyond silly, but I got used to it) and the intense Mark Randolph Hawkmore. <br /><br />Literally from the first sentence of this novel, the sexual chemistry and heat generated by these two characters is enough to render a person speechless. Okay, it rendered *me* speechless at least. There is a lot of sex in this book, especially early on. And, as it has been brought up by nearly everyone writing a review for this book, the sex scenes are incredibly vivid and detailed, and they along with the language may bother some readers. This is most definitely an historical erotica novel, with a BIG emphasis on the erotica part.<br /><br />And while I was thoroughly enjoying the passion and naughtiness of this story, something happened round about 200 pages in. This book became less about blistering sex scenes, and much more about the intense, bone-deep love that the two characters felt for each other. The last third of this book broke my heart, and literally reduced me to a weepy mess. <br /><br />Now that I have read Passion I see why it means so much to so many people. If you take the time to look past the vivid sensuality of the early parts of this book, you will find one of the most beautiful and deeply moving love stories I have ever read. I hope more people will open themselves up to this reading experience, because I'm so glad I did and this will definitely be a story I will never forget.<br /><br /><br />*more reviews at my blog*<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ravingbookaddict.blogspot.com/">http://ravingbookaddict.blogspot.com/</a></span>

  <span id="freeText8226710802627212045" style="display:none">Well. I don't even know what to say about this book. I spent all night thinking about what my review would be. I tossed and turned. How odd is that? I gave it 3 stars but I could have given it 1 or I could have given it 5. I just don't know how to rate a book that had parts that I really disliked and parts that I really liked. I guess a 3 star rating is fair for a book that brought out such emotions on both sides of the spectrum.<br /><br />The best way I know how to do this is list out all my likes and dislikes. She can write the hell out of a sex scene. So descriptive.<br />2. The emotions this books brings forth. I felt their pain. I was very angry for Mark and the sacrifice he was making. I hated his mom and Abigail. I felt for Charlotte who turned out to be a great character. And Passion, her way of seizing what she wanted, if only for a short time, was admirable.<br />3. Very good plot. Sometimes I wanted to brush away the sex just to get back to the plot. That is kind of rare for me.<br />4. Patience, Primrose and Matt. What interesting stories they will have.<br /><br /><br />Dislikes: <br />1. The word quim. Negative Ghostrider. Make it stop.<br />2. All the crying. I don't think I have even cried that much in my life. And for Mark to cry so much kind of bugged me. Put on your big boy briefs, buddy. Suck it up.<br />3. The use of exclamation points. When I read a sentence with an exclamation point it sounds very dramatic, in my head. This story had a ton of them. So there was always overacting and extra emotion. It seemed a tad overdone.<br />4. The epilogue. Come on, folks. I have nursed 2 kids for a decent amount of time and NEVER EVER did I consider doing THAT during the actual nursing of my kid. Gross and ew. No, thank you. Two compeletely separate acts in my head. Total turnoff.</span>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3191182-maureen-feeney?shelf=erotic">erotic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3191182-maureen-feeney?shelf=may-erotic-challange">may-erotic-challange</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer95834418&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95834418" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12212600550442525501">After skimming through the other reviews it amazes me that nearly everyone has a different view on this book, myself included. While most people had a problem with the first part of the book , I didn't my gripe was with the second half. <br/><br/>I found that this book was in 2 halves lust and love, the first half was the 2 strangers drawn together only by lust and sex. The sex scenes are plenty and though the sex acts ,positions etc are what you read in most Hist/Rom (most books have oral sex etc) the di</span>
  <span id="freeText12212600550442525501" style="display:none">After skimming through the other reviews it amazes me that nearly everyone has a different view on this book, myself included. While most people had a problem with the first part of the book , I didn't my gripe was with the second half. <br /><br />I found that this book was in 2 halves lust and love, the first half was the 2 strangers drawn together only by lust and sex. The sex scenes are plenty and though the sex acts ,positions etc are what you read in most Hist/Rom (most books have oral sex etc) the differance here is the graphic blunt wording. LV throws in enough f%^k's, c&amp;*ks and c$#ts etc to make you gasp. LV isn't just writing a loving sex scene she is writing about dirty sex. Afterall its about 2 people who want just anonymous raw sex without emotions, even though the descriptive dialogue can be OTT and repetitive at times it fits into the story.<br /><br />Then it changes for the second half of the book when the lust turns to love and the dirty sex scenes fade somewhat and it fitted perfectly with the story. I was wrapped up in Mark and Passion's story and so wanted them to have a HEA. LV ends the book honestly with not everyone being winners and I loved that. The cervix thing annoyed me would he know of a womans inners?, the man was an earl not a doctor. I think Mark got a bit too soft and weepy at the end and lost a bit of his edge and I wanted to yell at him. I was a bit annoyed that Passion was going to sacrifice everything for her cousin. If she loved her cousin that much why would she put her in a loveless marriage (like she had) to a man she knew loved her? A man she loved in return and was pregnant to? Didn't get that. I thought the entire story gelled together well and the lust part of the story didn't bother me. Scenes Kind of reminded me of Eloisa James duchess series. Because it is a great debut and I was gripped to see how it would all end I gave it 4*.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7522302390307027634">Extremely extremely ridiculous. And that's why I'm giving it 4 stars. As I was reading this, I kept wondering how the sexual acts described for anatomically possible and it led me to more thoroughly research uteri. I was already read up on the various pelvis shapes, you know, for identification of corpses/skeletons, but I learned so many new things about uteri positions due to this book. Anyway. This book is ridiculous, but it made me laugh and I've not read anything like it before, hence it rec</span>
  <span id="freeText7522302390307027634" style="display:none">Extremely extremely ridiculous. And that's why I'm giving it 4 stars. As I was reading this, I kept wondering how the sexual acts described for anatomically possible and it led me to more thoroughly research uteri. I was already read up on the various pelvis shapes, you know, for identification of corpses/skeletons, but I learned so many new things about uteri positions due to this book. Anyway. This book is ridiculous, but it made me laugh and I've not read anything like it before, hence it receives more stars just for being original. Or at least original to me. <br /><br />Oddly, this is book is all about the smut, smut, and MORE smut during the first half and then it's really romantic. You'll feel like you're reading two different books because after the first half of the book and drama occurs, it's all about the feels and romance. <br /><br />Just a warning to the wise, the next book, Patience, it sucks horribly. I hated it beyond hate.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91843899?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adrienne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adrienne" href="/user/show/2087365-adrienne">Adrienne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91843899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1511937550187067063">************possible spoilers**************************<br/><br/><br/>Ooohhh I finished tis late last night and went to sleep a very happy woman, but wondering how I could possibly write a review that conveys adequately exactly how this book made me feel. I've gone over all my emotions and feel what you end up reading here may seem, well,...... oh make your own minds up:)<br/><br/>Mark and Passion and their story is wonderful,full of lust, and love, whispered and declared in hushed tones whilst the world goes on around </span>
  <span id="freeText1511937550187067063" style="display:none">************possible spoilers**************************<br /><br /><br />Ooohhh I finished tis late last night and went to sleep a very happy woman, but wondering how I could possibly write a review that conveys adequately exactly how this book made me feel. I've gone over all my emotions and feel what you end up reading here may seem, well,...... oh make your own minds up:)<br /><br />Mark and Passion and their story is wonderful,full of lust, and love, whispered and declared in hushed tones whilst the world goes on around them unknowing. Their lust and love is never cheap or tawdry never arrogant or brash. They are (for me) a perfect couple and despite a terrible wrong~doing they remain at all times all of things above and more. There are never any TSTL moments, no words shouted in anger at one another, that could cut deep and wound, there is just a deep feeling of compassion and passion from both of them. Mark never flaunts his reputation to Passion but we know he has one, he is a dangerous man (sexually) who takes what he wants when he needs it and Passion is a heroine, who, manages to retain an aura of elegance and charm and discreetness whilst being outrageously wanton for Mark when the situation is 'appropriate' in the telling of their story for her to be like that. <br /> This book is deeply moving especially the scenes in the last third of the book which had me pressing my fingertips into my eyes to stop the stinging tears.<br /><br />So if like a story filled to the brim with lust, and love and passion that also has the ability to make you cry this may be for you.<br /><br /> <br /><br /></span>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/750368-maricar?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/750368-maricar?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54844467" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9844904462592293964">Excuse me while I recover from being scorched…<br/><br/>This was the first romance story that literally made me go, “Hot DAMN!” on the first words of the very first chapter. And then all tingly the rest of the way.<br/><br/>I know a lot of romance buffs are either indifferent to, or even disdainful of, erotica. And they can be justified sometimes—most of the stories in this genre are simply mindless sex, with most bordering on “perverted” liaisons. (Well, what <i>may</i> pass as perversions to some, in any case.) Another </span>
  <span id="freeText9844904462592293964" style="display:none">Excuse me while I recover from being scorched…<br /><br />This was the first romance story that literally made me go, “Hot DAMN!” on the first words of the very first chapter. And then all tingly the rest of the way.<br /><br />I know a lot of romance buffs are either indifferent to, or even disdainful of, erotica. And they can be justified sometimes—most of the stories in this genre are simply mindless sex, with most bordering on “perverted” liaisons. (Well, what <i>may</i> pass as perversions to some, in any case.) Another reason is that the plot can be more improbable than anything else—circumstances were conceived just a little bit too conveniently for any “romantic” element to exist.<br /><br />However, for some reason I don’t know what, <i>Passion</i> really hooked me in. <br /><br />And, in the risk of being called randy, I confess to not being fed up with Mark and Passion’s sex bouts. They really do sizzle without that “icky” or tiring feel. Though I admit the risqué language and the viciousness of the emotion between Mark and his mother kinda surprised me in the first few instances…somehow these paled in comparison to the love story itself between the hero and the heroine. <br /><br />And I really like the “episode”-like vibe that Valdez churned out in every heading of a new chapter—I was in tenterhooks as to what will happen once the clandestine world of Mark and Passion collides with that of Charlotte’s. And I was most especially thrilled with the growing fervor that Mark had for Passion. I mean, what woman wouldn’t want to be needed like <i>that</i>?<br /><br />All-in-all, a feel good novel—this lustful story actually has “heart” and real conflict (<i>damn near made me cry, too</i>). Very <i>very</i> satisfying read for me… <br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer92674619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8471334646352297332">This book was recommended to me by a friend whose enthusiasm about the book was so great that I knew I must quickly get my hands on it and read it as soon as possible. I knew going into it that the book was supposedly very hot with some scorching sex scenes but at the same time had a great love story to go along with it. After reading <i>Passion</i> I can say with great confidence that it lived up to it's reputation and surpassed my expectations of it! 5 Smoking Hot Stars!!!<br/><br/>The story about Passion (our</span>
  <span id="freeText8471334646352297332" style="display:none">This book was recommended to me by a friend whose enthusiasm about the book was so great that I knew I must quickly get my hands on it and read it as soon as possible. I knew going into it that the book was supposedly very hot with some scorching sex scenes but at the same time had a great love story to go along with it. After reading <i>Passion</i> I can say with great confidence that it lived up to it's reputation and surpassed my expectations of it! 5 Smoking Hot Stars!!!<br /><br />The story about Passion (our heroine) and Mark (our hero) starts off with a bang! They meet for the first time at The Crystal Palace Exhibition and immediately have this undeniable attraction to each other. Passion has been a widow for two years and Mark awakens her desire with one touch. Her marriage had not been a happy one and her husband had taken his pleasures from the marriage bed but left her feeling like there should have been something more and she was always left feeling empty from the experience. Passion comes from a loving home with a father who is a vicar and two sisters, Patience and Prim.<br /><br />Mark is an alpha male if ever there was one! He knows what he wants and goes after it. He takes his pleasures when he wants and with whom he wants it with but never settles with one woman. His mother is a horribly rude and selfish creature and has involved him in a blackmail scheme concerning his brother Matt, whom he dearly loves and has a great relationship with. Mark is being forced to marry or his family will be scandalized by the secret that his brother is illegitimate. Since Matt doesn't know this secret Mark will do what he has to do to keep it this way.<br /><br />Mark and Passion begin having a physical relationship only, agreeing not to learn anything personal about one another. But during their clandestine encounters (that take place in public(!) at the Exhibition) they begin to feel like there is something more to their relationship than just the amazing and very satisfying sex that they have. But the other people in their lives have different plans for them; Passion's aunt is busy playing matchmaker and Mark's mother has him tied up in the blackmailing scheme. So Mark and Passion work through their feelings of doing what is right and trying to keep their loved ones from being hurt while at the same time denying their growing love for one another. <br /><br />The road to Mark and Passion's <i>happily ever after</i> is filled with some of <i>the</i> hottest sex scenes I've ever read, desire, joy, laughter and even a tissue full of tears and then eventually love!<br /><br />Look for the sequel to this book, <i>Patience</i> comes out in April 2010 about Passion's sister and Mark's brother!!<br /><br /><b>***very explicit language and sexual details***</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8471334646352297332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_845922708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/845922708" />
    <a title="Delta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17814815-delta"><img alt="Delta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370478743p2/17814815.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/845922708?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Delta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Delta" href="/user/show/17814815-delta">Delta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101090718" href="/book/show/7558806-passion">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17814815-delta?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17814815-delta?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17814815-delta?shelf=half-star">half-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17814815-delta?shelf=erotica">erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17814815-delta?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17814815-delta?shelf=dark-romance">dark-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17814815-delta?shelf=oh-the-angst">oh-the-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17814815-delta?shelf=lies-lies-lies">lies-lies-lies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer845922708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14567256737060855401"><i>
  <b>3.5 Angsty-Explicit-Victorian Stars</b>
</i><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80760.Passion__Passion_Quartet___1_' title='Passion (Passion Quartet, #1) by Lisa Valdez' rel='nofollow noopener'>Passion</a> is a vicar's daughter and a young, beautify widow. When she encounters the hero for the first time--in a public place and without introduction--she inexplicably abandons her standards of restraint and morality to have sex with this stranger in the very public setting (although out of sight). <br/><br/>Mark, the Eighth Earl of Langley, is a truly insufferable, selfish prick (really the only word that fits him, and I do not usually sink to such language in my r</span>
  <span id="freeText14567256737060855401" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>3.5 Angsty-Explicit-Victorian Stars</b>
</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80760.Passion__Passion_Quartet___1_" title="Passion (Passion Quartet, #1) by Lisa Valdez" rel="nofollow noopener">Passion</a> is a vicar's daughter and a young, beautify widow. When she encounters the hero for the first time--in a public place and without introduction--she inexplicably abandons her standards of restraint and morality to have sex with this stranger in the very public setting (although out of sight). <br /><br />Mark, the Eighth Earl of Langley, is a truly insufferable, selfish prick (really the only word that fits him, and I do not usually sink to such language in my reviews) who only becomes sympathetic at the point that he realizes that he loves Passion--selfishly in that he needs her. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>The hero did WHAT to her?</i>
</b><br /><br />The erotic scenes are really disturbing in that (with her consent) Mark forcefully batters his way into her body so that her cervix gives way and her womb tilts, allowing his oversized member all the way in. This process happens in multiple scenes and seems so violent that one would think it would cause severe, if not fatal, internal injuries to a woman.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>...And she let him???</i>
</b><br /><br />Only deep self loathing would allow a woman to be used and abused as Passion was by Mark with no promise of a relationship or support of any kind outside of the bedroom. Especially in that time period (1851), Passion risked everything to participate in a no-strings sexual relationship with Mark.<br /><br />Nonetheless, the angst and longing between the H/h pulled me in, and I cared enough about the characters to stick around for the HEA. The secondary character I would like to see more of is Mark's brother, Matthew, who demonstrated empathy and compassion.<br /><br />This one is difficult to rate... not my kind of story because it had to do with heartbreak caused by lies told to cover up infidelity (although not infidelity of H/h, Mark and Passion). The story seems to be more about the sex than anything else, and the sex preceded any relationship. <br /><br />The tone of the book seems to fall in the middle between a dark romance and a typical Victorian HEA, but without (for me) the satisfaction level of either. I believe the satisfaction is diminished because the <i>primary</i> reason that Mark seems to love Passion is because her body can accommodate his 10-1/2 inch monster you-know-what, although an additional reason is revealed near the end of the story.<br /><br />If you like your historic romance on the darker side and with graphic sex scenes, you may enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80760.Passion__Passion_Quartet___1_" title="Passion (Passion Quartet, #1) by Lisa Valdez" rel="nofollow noopener">Passion</a>. I will try at least one more book in the <i>Passion Quartet</i> series and hope for a stronger heroine.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14567256737060855401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110301210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer301052070182555640"><b>My reviews are mostly my thoughts as I went with the book...</b><br/><br/>I didn't used to read erotica when I first read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80760.Passion__Passion_Quartet___1_' title='Passion (Passion Quartet, #1) by Lisa Valdez' rel='nofollow noopener'>Passion</a> but man, this was some great introductory book for me! When I first came across this one on a very ordinary day almost 2 yrs ago, I knew nothing about it; about all the debates of 'to read or not to read' or 'wow or eww'. I read no reviews, just picked it up because I was curious about the title ... So, when Mark saved Passion from that accident in the very beginning of the book, I</span>
  <span id="freeText301052070182555640" style="display:none"><b>My reviews are mostly my thoughts as I went with the book...</b><br /><br />I didn't used to read erotica when I first read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80760.Passion__Passion_Quartet___1_" title="Passion (Passion Quartet, #1) by Lisa Valdez" rel="nofollow noopener">Passion</a> but man, this was some great introductory book for me! When I first came across this one on a very ordinary day almost 2 yrs ago, I knew nothing about it; about all the debates of 'to read or not to read' or 'wow or eww'. I read no reviews, just picked it up because I was curious about the title ... So, when Mark saved Passion from that accident in the very beginning of the book, I thought, <i>"oh well, I think he's going to find her out later and pursue her (as usual). I hope he's an obsessive hero"</i>. Well, what a hero he turned out to be! And I guessed right. Well, sort of! I remember that the beginning was every bit magnetic as Mark and Passion's affair. I also remember daydreaming about the love scenes while doing my MA classes. I'm glad I didn't start teaching back then, lmao. Just think how I would've looked daydreaming about Mark while attending my students, ahemm! Well, moving on...<br /><br />Although Mark and Passion's affair started off very physical, even in the first love scene I felt the bond was there. I won't go into details since people tend to interpret all these in various ways and there are more than one elaborate review can be found in GR. I was in doubt myself for quite a while but there were a few scenes in this book made me cry or wistful. One was the scene where Mark cries while Passion holds him close (read and find out, it was heart wrenching, his need and love for Passion was so great.)<br /><br />I read a review of this book in a blog just after I finished it. It was so wickedly funny, had me in stitches! The reviewer liked it and so did I. I've read the book many times over afterwards (don't ask which parts I've read the most, I think it's kinda obvious *blushes*) and continued to be absolutely fascinated every time I did ... Hope this makes sense. Suffice to say, I've <i>learned</i> a lot from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80760.Passion__Passion_Quartet___1_" title="Passion (Passion Quartet, #1) by Lisa Valdez" rel="nofollow noopener">Passion</a>! ;)<br /><br />PS: I didn't have to wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80761.Patience__Passion_Quartet___2_" title="Patience (Passion Quartet, #2) by Lisa Valdez" rel="nofollow noopener">Patience</a> too long I guess. Matthew sounded so very intriguing, I would've died if I ... never mind! lolz</span>
  <a data-text-id="301052070182555640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16343015587552547667">What can I say but HOT! STEAMY! SEXY! OMG! I got pulled into the story from the very beginning. Though it started off like an erotic novel, the author slowly weaves the romance into the story. I was anxious, quickly trying to figure out when the main characters were going to find out that they knew each other more then they realized. I liked the heroine(but not her ridiculous name) and felt for her once she discovered she was in love with (the hero) and could not have him. I felt torn for her. H</span>
  <span id="freeText16343015587552547667" style="display:none">What can I say but HOT! STEAMY! SEXY! OMG! I got pulled into the story from the very beginning. Though it started off like an erotic novel, the author slowly weaves the romance into the story. I was anxious, quickly trying to figure out when the main characters were going to find out that they knew each other more then they realized. I liked the heroine(but not her ridiculous name) and felt for her once she discovered she was in love with (the hero) and could not have him. I felt torn for her. However it took longer for me to like the Hero. I sometimes found him to be crude but once he finally discovered his own feelings and let go, I was moved. The ending was quite emotional and it definitely had the “sighing” moments as I like to call it. I was so thrilled for the couple. <br />Now as much as I could rave about this book there was some bad points (not enough for me to dislike the book). Though I’m not particularly fond of having the sex scenes right off the bat, I happened to not mind this so much in the book. In fact, I found it interesting enough that though there was a lot of sex in this book, I still felt the two characters were connecting somehow. But there was a sex scene where the author mentioned cervix too much! If I wasn’t reading this on my kindle, I would have taken a permanent black marker and definitely marked it out. Oh, also the word “womb" which sexually was creeping me out. Then there was the constant cursing. I have a potty mouth so of course I can understand the cursing but even I was like please stop it.<br />Overall I really enjoyed this book and look forward to Patience and Matthew’s story. The little teaser that I’ve read drew me in quickly and now I can’t wait to see what happens next. <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText51578086032766840" style="display:none">Let me preface this by saying, WHAT THE EVER LOVING FUCK IS THIS BOOK DOING TO MEE!?<br /><br />I have never read a historical romance bordering so much on erotica before. There's a difference between smutty historical romane and an erotica historical romance... and ohmygod, how I am all in for this!<br /><br />First chapter in, I was left gobsmacked and hot and bothered. Mind you, the chemistry between these two people were off the charts!<br /><br /><i>
  <b>His hand tightened in her hair. “I need to be a part of you. Tell me you’ll let me. Tell me you won’t say hold.” Every muscle in his body wanted to drive into her. “Because once I start fucking you, I swear to God, I’m not stopping.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Not only it was crazy hot, it also packed that emotional punch right to your heart (and vagina in some scenes 😉). I haven't feel that heart-broken ever since I read that end scene in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/330721.Dreaming_of_You__The_Gamblers_of_Craven_s___2_" title="Dreaming of You (The Gamblers of Craven's, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreaming of You</a>. You felt the hopelessness of these characters and damn if I didn't shed an ugly cry when it happened. What is it about star-crossed lovers that always destroyed me.<br /><br /><i>
  <b><br />"And what of my suffering? Suffering, in the face of which, you expect me to be noble and honorable. Suffering I’m supposed to bear over a lifetime with equanimity and grace. I’m not the bloody Savior, Passion. I’m a man. And I will not crucify myself on the altar of your morality!”<br /><br />“Once, long ago, I begged for love. I swore I would never do it again. But I’m begging you now, Passion. Please, love me.”<br /></b>
</i><br /><br />Sigh... I think I just found my next bingeable author.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186041012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8391082496190078078">This book is one of those that causes quite a bit of heated reaction from readers- both love and hate. Whereas when I first read it I would have definitely fallen more in the former than the latter category- as I think back on it, I'm much more ambivalent about my reactions. <br/><br/>On the the one hand I found it, Sexy, explicit, and yes romantic I thought it was a good read. For me the plot seemed simple and intriguing at the same time. The conflict was not hidden- except from the two leads and I waite</span>
  <span id="freeText8391082496190078078" style="display:none">This book is one of those that causes quite a bit of heated reaction from readers- both love and hate. Whereas when I first read it I would have definitely fallen more in the former than the latter category- as I think back on it, I'm much more ambivalent about my reactions. <br /><br />On the the one hand I found it, Sexy, explicit, and yes romantic I thought it was a good read. For me the plot seemed simple and intriguing at the same time. The conflict was not hidden- except from the two leads and I waited on pins and needles till they finally figured out what was going on behind the scenes. I was anxious, not because of the conflict, but because I wanted to see how they would react. If they over or under reacted it would ruin the book for me. Fortunately the author played it perfectly!<br /><br />On the other? The sex bits. Don’t get me wrong- it's hot stuff and I loved that she didn’t shy from explicitness, but there were times where I thought it was slightly annoying. C’mon, how many times can you have sex in the same OPEN place without being caught? (Apparently as much as you want according to this book.) And the size of his schlong?? wowzers!<br /><br />Recently I’ve been frustrated with the historical romance genre. Inundated with turdball, clichéd, overused plots, the genre is all but over for me. Unfortunately, or fortunately for the publishers, I pick up enough like Passion to keep me coming back.<br /><br />I’m giving this one 4 out of 5.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97391224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9749383768668789125">I picked up this gem after seeing it rated so highly among erotica fans. And let me tell you this is a hot and steamy. <i>Passion</i> takes naughty smexing and dirty talk to a new level. From reviews, I knew the c-word was common, but Lord Almighty that was just the tip of the iceberg. At times it was completely titillating and others a bit crude for my taste. However, somewhere along the way Passion and Mark’s story evolved into so much more than sex. It became the heart-felt love story about a man an</span>
  <span id="freeText9749383768668789125" style="display:none">I picked up this gem after seeing it rated so highly among erotica fans. And let me tell you this is a hot and steamy. <i>Passion</i> takes naughty smexing and dirty talk to a new level. From reviews, I knew the c-word was common, but Lord Almighty that was just the tip of the iceberg. At times it was completely titillating and others a bit crude for my taste. However, somewhere along the way Passion and Mark’s story evolved into so much more than sex. It became the heart-felt love story about a man and woman who, beneath a veil of secrecy and deception, discovered a love and passion they had long thought unattainable. The more I read, the more I became enthralled in Passion and Mark’s story and eagerly awaited their happily ever after, which came with the same passion and intensity as it started.<br /><br />While the language and dialogue might be a bit racy and shocking to some, the story altogether is filled with enough raw emotion and touching moments to make it well worth the read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9749383768668789125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nNZvT4puHsDtLxZ+sE1tOS/rHfhIZkRqp/6gKh1dztfMPJmdewD9il3urcVOxbcl25qWW65L8j/qWTn5C0IfjQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IWXVIMP3tEH0VnyYXk2IpKxnQNwvhOqE+e1fwMv3jDRxjyPyMplXC0SXxyOgxVK4WBbLf8mpXNG0SsYT3ehdbg==')})
  }
